< Review>
Drove this road at midnight and it was ok. Only went because there was no other cars and not much you can do during midnight in San Francisco. I don't think it'll be worth the tourist traffic but glad I got to experience it. Since there was no traffic, it took is 1-2 minutes to complete the drive. Not as difficult as it may intimidate.</Review>

< Text>
One of San Francisco's most popular landmark. There are always people at the bottom of the street taking photos. We have been here many times during different seasons.
May - Quite cold although almost approaching summer, flowers are starting to bloom. Nice to make a trip down this road to experience the ride on the "Crookedest Street in the World".
June - Nicest weather to come as it is not too cold, the flowers are blooming so it is best for photos.< /Text>

<username>Cook & Fly<//username><time>1597825535053<//time><rate>4< /rate>< Text>
@cooknfly
Lombard street is one of the MUST see spots in the city or at least pass by like we did, there is no place to sit and have a coffee but you can definetly stop and take a photo in the middle of the street if it aint too crowded, the best time of the day to go and get that perfect photo is from 6 amto 8 am if you go after this time it will be crowded and it will be hard to make that nice instagramable shot.

Also if you stop by, make sure you do enjoy the little drive down hill, is extremely short and if you dont go slow you won‚Äôt enjoy it and will find it not worth it hehe, so drive slow, everyone there is for the same reason.

There Is no parking space usually during busy hours but try to drive around for like two to three blocks away so you can find a parking spot and walk back to Lombard to do your photos.

After visiting Lombard we went to Golden Gate and the port, good luck visiting San Francisco!

Overall : 8/10

For more content, checkout @cooknfly on Instagram.

Stay safe.<//Text>

<user>106881351674762933062</user><username>Aleksandar Tadiƒá</username><Time>1593927914604<//Time>< rate>
5</rate>
<text>Lombard Street is an east‚Äìwest street in San Francisco, California that is famous for a steep, one-block section with eight hairpin turns. Stretching from The Presidio east to The Embarcadero (with a gap on Telegraph Hill), most of the street's western segment is a major thoroughfare designated as part of U.S. Route 101. The famous one-block section, claimed to be "the crookedest street in the world", is located along the eastern segment in the Russian Hill neighborhood. It is a major tourist attraction, receiving around two million visitors per year and up to 17,000 per day on busy summer weekends, as of 2015.< /text>< Pictures>

(Translated by Google) Lombard Street San Francisco:
Today Lombard is one of the most visited sites in the city. Its construction was completed in 1922, and it is a beautiful street descending from a hill to the bottom in many curves decorated with trees and flowers. Lombard Street is famous for being the most winding and most beautiful street in the world.

< Review>
Had gel polish pedicure yesterday for $26 (I paid by card so $1 more than if I'd paid in cash). My technician was super-friendly and meticulous. It is a no-frill store on 24th st. surrounded by awesome Latin American eateries! The staff are all Vietnamese and friendly as far as I saw, but a customer came in later and started yelling at the staff for not having time to do her nails. It was pretty clear nobody wanted to serve the loud/rude customer, but eventually they agreed to do her nails. I mean this store has probably a more diverse clientele than most nail saloons in other SF neighborhoods.  And, if you want a spa experience, this is not it! All I was looking for was a place that's friendly, affordable and quick, so this worked out well! Will go there again.</Review>

< text>
The staff is very friendly, but this was the worst manicure I've ever received. I got gels, which for me usually last at least 2-3 weeks. The very next day one of the nails had already started chipping after just taking a shower. Four days later almost every nail had started to completely peel off. Very disappointing. Also, not a good pedi experience. I can't believe they charge the same for pedicures as other salons when they don't do even the most basic scrub or massage, etc. One of the nails smudged during my mani and they just painted over the big smudge. I asked for them to smooth it out, and they were happy to, but it still wasn't a good job. $16 isn't a lot for a pedi, but it looked like I'd done it myself. Sadly, This was my first and last time at Sandy's. I definitely wouldn't recommend.</text>

Whoa! This gotta b unique in the region considering all the popular Desi desserts under Innovative menu. Falooda tops it all with other delicacies especially Gola Ganda, Cham Cham, Kulfi. Unbelievable stuff under one nice clean n cozy roof.

Just tried Doodh Patti on my 2nd visit. Not at all near anywhere the Original. Completely Americanized... Tasteless, Odorless.

Tried Gola Ganda on my 3rd visit... It was good no doubt. The only downside is that the shaved ice starts to bond together to a lump form... Now u gotta shovel job! The Date shake is absolutely non-authentic and actually pathetic the way they are doin it. It's a disgrace to this Arabic Smoothie.

Tried Bun Kabab on my 4th visit.... is there anything they are messin' up with!? Very desi touch... hot! takes you back to school days!

Tried Bihari Roll on my 5th visit... V inexpensive n even though need improvement still not bad...

Tried Mango Shake on my 6th visit... Completely fake shake...! they couldn't even make the shake look at least yellow... It was a white Mango Shake!.. No taste either... What a waste!

7th Visit... Tried Pakola Float. Pretty ordinary.

8th Visit... Tried Coke Float... They r better off not makin these Fake Luquid Delicacies

<rating>3< /rating>< review>
I've passed by this place a couple times, as my coworkers like to come to this plaza for lunch, but never went in until now.

Scoops N Scoops is a nitrogen ice cream place, so the prices are more expensive.

When I walked in, I noticed their LED display menu was not done well. They explained their process, but they don't have a list of flavors on there. You have to grab a menu from the counter to read what flavors they offer. Service is also a little slow. Had to wait at the counter for a while before someone came up to help me.

I got the red velvet flavor with brownie bits. You have the option of having the topping being mixed in or on top. The cashier who rung me up told me that mixing in was a lot better, but when I got my ice cream, I noticed the brownie bits got hard. Next time, I would definitely opt to get my toppings on top instead of mixed in. Taste wise, I could really taste the red velvet flavor and the ice cream was very creamy.</review>

<user_id>111786517743281339317</user_id>< Text>
I tried both the strawberry ice cream sandwiched between two macaron shells and the black sesame red bean & mochi creation, and both were quite disappointing.

While I liked the shells of the macarons, the ice cream did not taste any different than a regular strawberry ice cream that I would find at the grocery store. The black sesame did not taste like black sesame at all, and instead tasted more like peanut butter. The red beans were too mushy, and the combination did not go well together.

I've heard a few good things about Scoops N Scoops, so perhaps the items we ordered were the wrong ones.<//Text>

<user_name>Daniel Jenkins<//user_name><Time>1447718126433< /Time><Rating>2< /Rating>< Text>
Menu items are interesting, but it seems like whoever created them didn't try them before they started selling them. The cotton candy dish was essentially preventing you from eating the ice cream until the cotton candy was gone. One of my friends got an item that came with a cookie, and it came on a totally separate plate; not with ice cream on it like a pizookie or something. The creme brulee is heated on top of the ice cream, so the sugar part essentially melts off the top of the ice cream (half of mine slid out of the cup and onto the plate before I even started eating). Prices are high, and customer service was weak - the manager (yes, manager) offered to get our table waters, which we gladly accepted... no waters were received. That being said, the flavors are good, and there are options here that aren't available at some of the other liquid nitrogen ice cream places around, so they're just finding their footing. May be worth a try if they make some changes, but until then, I'm sticking with Creamistry or Cauldron for my nitrogen-based ice cream.<//Text>
